Benkongerike

**Benkongerike** is a medium-sized [cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Caves "Skyrim:Caves") southeast of [Saering's Watch](/wiki/Skyrim:Saering%27s_Watch "Skyrim:Saering's Watch") containing [bristlebacks](/wiki/Skyrim:Bristleback "Skyrim:Bristleback") and [rieklings](/wiki/Skyrim:Riekling "Skyrim:Riekling"). It contains two zones: *[Benkongerike](#Benkongerike)* and *[Benkongerike Great Hall](#Benkongerike_Great_Hall)*.

Its [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") teaches part of the [Cyclone](/wiki/Skyrim:Cyclone "Skyrim:Cyclone") [dragon shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts").

## Related Quests

- **[Black Book](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Book_(quest) "Skyrim:Black Book (quest)")**: Retrieve a Black Book from a dungeon.
- **[Black Book: Untold Legends](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Book:_Untold_Legends_(quest) "Skyrim:Black Book: Untold Legends (quest)")**: Learn the [Black Book](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Book:_Untold_Legends_(book) "Skyrim:Black Book: Untold Legends (book)")'s hidden knowledge.
- **[Lost Knowledge](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Knowledge "Skyrim:Lost Knowledge")**: Retrieve the [Black Books](/wiki/Lore:Black_Book "Lore:Black Book") for [Neloth](/wiki/Skyrim:Neloth "Skyrim:Neloth").
- **[Pain in the Necklace](/wiki/Skyrim:Pain_in_the_Necklace "Skyrim:Pain in the Necklace")**: Find [East Empire pendants](/wiki/Skyrim:East_Empire_Pendant "Skyrim:East Empire Pendant") for [Fethis Alor](/wiki/Skyrim:Fethis_Alor "Skyrim:Fethis Alor").

### Exterior

From the Headwaters of Harstrad, follow the path to the northwest, and when you reach a junction, turn left to the southwest. You eventually pass under an arch consisting of two columns with a large slab on top. On your right is a statue with unusable barrels and crates. There is a food barrel to the right of the entrance, and a novice-locked chest to the left.

### Benkongerike

As soon as you enter, you will be in a snowy tunnel descending to the northwest. As soon as the passage levels out, there is a narrow tunnel on your right that twists and turns and eventually leads to a novice-locked chest and two [burial urns](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn"). There is also a hidden door next to the chest that will act as a shortcut back from the end of this cave system. At the end of the initial tunnel is a riekling tent with a [deer pelt](/wiki/Skyrim:Deer_Pelt "Skyrim:Deer Pelt") inside and a piece of [firewood](/wiki/Skyrim:Firewood "Skyrim:Firewood") to the left. A tunnel on the left leads into a large cavern.

First cavern

In the cavern, you can see three large pillars (all leaning over), a nearby riekling camp consisting of two riekling huts and a riekling tent, and various crates, barrels, and sacks all around the room below you. Two more riekling tents can be seen in the distance. There are three rieklings running about that you can see. The path down is on your right, and follows the wall around the cavern to place you beside a riekling hut to your right. A tent to your left contains a bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"). To the right of the tent is the second hut, and beside this hut is a bottle of alto wine, a [pine thrush egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Pine_Thrush_Egg "Skyrim:Pine Thrush Egg"), two bulbs of [garlic](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic "Skyrim:Garlic"), and a medium [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse"), all beside and on top of a crate. In the middle of this area among more crates is a large [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn").

Bristleback

On your right as you move through the cavern heading south, past the first riekling hut are two large urns and two burial urns lined up in a row against the rocks. Just past these urns is another hut to the right. Behind this hut are some large mammoth ribcages, and to the left are two more large urns by a fence behind one of the pillars. In front of the same pillar is yet another tent, with an archery target inside, and a large urn and a [gourd](/wiki/Skyrim:Gourd "Skyrim:Gourd") to the right. To the left (west) is a tall lookout platform with a riekling on guard and a bristleback wandering around the bottom, next to another tent to the left. This tent has a burial urn inside, a large urn to the left, and an open crate containing two samples of [imp stool](/wiki/Skyrim:Imp_Stool "Skyrim:Imp Stool") and a sample of [Namira's rot](/wiki/Skyrim:Namira%27s_Rot "Skyrim:Namira's Rot") in front. Beside the fence and pillar to the right of the platform is another tent. Inside this tent is a sample of [wheat](/wiki/Skyrim:Wheat "Skyrim:Wheat"), three [steel ingots](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Ingot "Skyrim:Steel Ingot") hidden under a kettle, and a sack. To the left of the tent is a barrel with a pair of weightless [shoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Shoes "Skyrim:Shoes") on top, with a [bowl](/wiki/Skyrim:Bowl "Skyrim:Bowl") and a [goblet](/wiki/Skyrim:Goblet "Skyrim:Goblet") on a nearby crate (see [bugs](#Bugs)). Returning to the area near the entrance of this first cavern, to the left along the southeast wall is a statue with an unlit brazier in front holding an [iron helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Helmet "Skyrim:Iron Helmet"). To the right is a tent with the usual crates, barrels, and sacks piled on either side and a [drum](/wiki/Skyrim:Drum "Skyrim:Drum") in front. To the right are two barrels and a crate, with an empty random soul gem and a [silver necklace](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Necklace "Skyrim:Silver Necklace") on top. Between these items and the tunnel onward are three large urns and two burial urns. The tunnel onward leading south is to the right.

Following the tunnel south, it becomes an icy passage. At the end is a food barrel with a piece of large [charcoal](/wiki/Skyrim:Charcoal "Skyrim:Charcoal") on top, and three samples of wheat, a bowl, and two more burial urns on the ground beside it. The tunnel turns to the west, passing a rock on the right with a flute on top, then a [knapsack](/wiki/Skyrim:Knapsack "Skyrim:Knapsack") and two large urns on your left beside a large rock. The tunnel then turns to the north and becomes a ledge above another cavern, where there are three rieklings. In front of the ledge is a platform with a ramp down to the cavern floor. On your right on the ledge is an alcove holding two large urns, an unlocked chest with a deer pelt to the left of it, and a [pickaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickaxe "Skyrim:Pickaxe"). At the end of the ledge in the northeastern corner is a riekling hut, beside which is a large urn, a deer pelt, a sample of [scaly pholiota](/wiki/Skyrim:Scaly_Pholiota "Skyrim:Scaly Pholiota"), some [hawk feathers](/wiki/Skyrim:Hawk_Feathers "Skyrim:Hawk Feathers"), a sample of [white cap](/wiki/Skyrim:White_Cap "Skyrim:White Cap"), and an [apothecary's satchel](/wiki/Skyrim:Apothecary%27s_Satchel "Skyrim:Apothecary's Satchel"). A wooden plate to the left of the hut holds some slaughterfish scales and a large piece of charcoal. Farther west is another tent containing two wooden plates holding a bulb of garlic, a filled random [soul gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems"), and a [flawless sapphire](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Sapphire "Skyrim:Flawless Sapphire").

Underneath the ramp down is an unlocked [strongbox](/wiki/Skyrim:Strongbox "Skyrim:Strongbox") and a cast iron pot containing a [thistle branch](/wiki/Skyrim:Thistle_Branch "Skyrim:Thistle Branch"). The cavern continues to the west. Against the southern wall is a [salt pile](/wiki/Skyrim:Salt_Pile "Skyrim:Salt Pile") beside a chair. To the west is a large rock with a bucket containing eight loose coins and a rock warbler egg. Beneath this rock is an iron helmet. In the southwestern corner is a tent with an [iron mace](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Mace "Skyrim:Iron Mace") in a kettle, with an urn beside the tent. To the right along the wall next to a large rock with an animal skull displayed on top are two food sacks, with two bottles of alto wine among them. The cavern turns to the northwest, with a tent to the right with a fire in front of it. Around the fire are two [ash yams](/wiki/Skyrim:Ash_Yam "Skyrim:Ash Yam"), two sheaves of wheat, and two [rabbit haunches](/wiki/Skyrim:Rabbit_Haunch "Skyrim:Rabbit Haunch"). To the left of the tent, beside the next tunnel is a drum and a large carved stone head.

An ice tunnel continues to the northwest and descends to another tent. Just before reaching the tent, a [riekling barrel](/wiki/Skyrim:Riekling_Barrel "Skyrim:Riekling Barrel") on the right will burst open, revealing a riekling. At the end of this tunnel, a riekling is hiding in a bush to the left of the tent, which contains two pieces of firewood. To the left is a woodcutter's axe in a kettle, and to the right, on a rock under some clutter, is a [snow fox pelt](/wiki/Skyrim:Snow_Fox_Pelt "Skyrim:Snow Fox Pelt"). The tunnel turns to the northeast and continues to descend. Take care, as there is a [tripwire](/wiki/Skyrim:Tripwire "Skyrim:Tripwire") ahead that triggers a [claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Claw "Skyrim:Claw") trap, hinged on the left. Just past the tripwire, an alcove on the left has a tent with a riekling barrel in front. Inside the tent is a pair of [iron boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Boots "Skyrim:Iron Boots"), and two urns flank the tent. Past this alcove is a second tripwire that triggers another claw trap, hinged on the right. By the claw on the right is a riekling hut, and to the left of the hut is a stone bowl containing a [Dibella statue](/wiki/Skyrim:Dibella_Statue "Skyrim:Dibella Statue"). Farther to the left is a large rock with a knapsack, a [potion of cure disease](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Cure_Disease "Skyrim:Potion of Cure Disease"), an ash yam in a cast iron pot, and a salt pile. The tunnel ends to the northeast with an urn and some riekling spears on a crate, and a riekling hidden in the snow. There is another tunnel heading to the northwest, with a tripwire at the start of the tunnel triggering another claw trap, hinged from above. The tunnel turns back to the northeast and opens into another cavern.

Bridges

Flooded cavern

You will enter this cavern on a ledge, with bridges ahead joining several platforms, ledges, and columns, and a ramp down to the cavern floor below on the left. On the right is a bucket containing a [woodcutter's axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Woodcutter%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Woodcutter's Axe"), a [chef's hat](/wiki/Skyrim:Chef%27s_Hat "Skyrim:Chef's Hat"), and a [chef's tunic](/wiki/Skyrim:Chef%27s_Tunic "Skyrim:Chef's Tunic"). Below, the cavern is partially flooded. On the ledges, quite a few rieklings are running about. Crossing the first bridge to the first platform, there are three bottles of alto wine, two bottles of [ale](/wiki/Skyrim:Ale "Skyrim:Ale"), and a [goat cheese wedge](/wiki/Skyrim:Goat_Cheese_Wedge "Skyrim:Goat Cheese Wedge") in a bucket. Two rieklings are on this platform. Across a second bridge heading southeast to the next platform, there is a [leg of goat](/wiki/Skyrim:Leg_of_Goat "Skyrim:Leg of Goat") and an unlocked chest hanging off the right side, with a drum to your left. Two more rieklings are in this area. Continuing to the southeast across another short bridge to a well-lit area, the next bridge is to the north. There are then two more bridges, the second of which bears to the northeast, where another riekling stands. The next bridge is to the southeast; it leads to the far side of the cavern and a ledge with a doorway to the east. There is an ash yam on a crate to the left by the bridge, and to the right of the doorway are five pieces of [clam meat](/wiki/Skyrim:Clam_Meat "Skyrim:Clam Meat") and two [pearls](/wiki/Skyrim:Pearl "Skyrim:Pearl"), most of which are in a bucket. From this ledge, there is also another bridge to the south to another ledge against the south wall, where another riekling stands and a ramp leads down to two [silver ore veins](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Silver Ore Vein") and a burial urn.

The best place to drop into the water is from the second silver ore vein, as a novice-locked chest sits beneath it. There are two more silver ore veins slightly west of the chest, behind a rock. The only other item of interest on the lower level is a random enchanted [greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Greatsword "Skyrim:Greatsword"), which is found between the ramp at the beginning of the cavern and the first platform. The sword is beside an unlootable skeleton at the narrowest part. This provides the easiest access to the ramp back up.

In the tunnel to the east, the architecture changes to that of a [Nordic barrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Ruins "Skyrim:Nordic Ruins"). At the end of this short corridor is an unlit brazier on a stone plinth containing a pair of random boots. A corridor to the north leads into a room with an iron door opposite. There are two goblets, a bowl, and a burial urn in the corridor. The room contains six barrels at the other end, three of which are actually riekling barrels which rieklings will burst from to ambush you. This will scatter a number of items around the room. There are two gourds, a rock warbler egg, three random potions, and two common books; some of these items may remain on a set of shelves in the room. The iron door leads to *Benkongerike Great Hall*.

### Benkongerike Great Hall

Through the door is another room, with a broken sideboard on your left and a piece of [quicksilver ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Quicksilver_Ore "Skyrim:Quicksilver Ore") in front. Farther along the left wall is a bookcase containing some riekling spears and four [random](/wiki/Skyrim:LItemBookClutter "Skyrim:LItemBookClutter") books. On the right side of the room is a riekling tent containing thirteen copies of *[The Lusty Argonian Maid, v1](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Lusty_Argonian_Maid,_v1 "Skyrim:The Lusty Argonian Maid, v1")* and six copies of *[v2](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Lusty_Argonian_Maid,_v2 "Skyrim:The Lusty Argonian Maid, v2")*, with a [Telekinesis](/wiki/Skyrim:Telekinesis "Skyrim:Telekinesis") [spell tome](/wiki/Skyrim:Spell_Tomes "Skyrim:Spell Tomes") hidden under them all. At the far end of the room are three large urns (two on the left, one on the right) and a doorway to an ascending wooden spiral staircase in the northern wall.

Riekling infestation

Climbing the staircase, there are still plenty of signs of rieklings, with painted symbols on the walls. At the top, the corridor heads north again. On the left, you pass some bars through which you can see a chest, two pedestals, and two urns. There is an open iron door on your right heading east. Opposite is an expert-locked iron door and some more bars farther along on the left. Through the locked door, the chest in front of you is unlocked, with the two urns on the far left. The left-hand pedestal holds a copy of the [Benkongerike Key](/wiki/Skyrim:Benkongerike_Key "Skyrim:Benkongerike Key"), and the other pedestal holds a copy of *[Dragon Language: Myth no More](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Language:_Myth_no_More "Skyrim:Dragon Language: Myth no More")*. Following the corridor to the east, there are two burial urns where it turns to the south. The room ahead opens into another large room on a balcony overlooking the floor below. There are bridges around this room joining platforms on top of columns. There are three rieklings and a [mounted riekling](/wiki/Skyrim:Mounted_Riekling "Skyrim:Mounted Riekling") in this room. On your left is an urn, and to the right are the wooden steps down.

At the bottom of the steps, ahead are two barrels in the room's northeast corner (see [bugs](#Bugs)). Under the steps is a [rock warbler egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Rock_Warbler_Egg "Skyrim:Rock Warbler Egg") and a [chicken's egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Chicken%27s_Egg "Skyrim:Chicken's Egg") on the ground. To the left is an open sarcophagus with a dead [draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers#Draugr "Skyrim:Containers") inside and a bulb of garlic on the northwestern edge of the sarcophagus, as well as a cast iron pot containing a [flute](/wiki/Skyrim:Flute "Skyrim:Flute") and [potato](/wiki/Skyrim:Potato "Skyrim:Potato"). Along the wall to the left is another sarcophagus, which has a [stalhrim](/wiki/Skyrim:Stalhrim "Skyrim:Stalhrim") deposit covering another dead draugr. The first pillar nearest the bottom of the stairs has a bucket with two pieces of [corundum ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Corundum_Ore "Skyrim:Corundum Ore") inside. The pillar to the right has a crate and a barrel beside it with a [torchbug thorax](/wiki/Skyrim:Torchbug_Thorax "Skyrim:Torchbug Thorax"), a bottle of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine"), and an [orange dartwing](/wiki/Skyrim:Orange_Dartwing "Skyrim:Orange Dartwing") on the crate, and a bowl of [bone meal](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Meal "Skyrim:Bone Meal") in a metal bowl on the barrel.

Against the east wall is a crate, with a medium coin purse on top and a sack beside it. To the right is a collapsed pillar, beside which are three [corundum ingots](/wiki/Skyrim:Corundum_Ingot "Skyrim:Corundum Ingot"), several pieces of cheese, a pair of [leather boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Leather_Boots "Skyrim:Leather Boots"), and on top of a barrel a [gold sapphire ring](/wiki/Skyrim:Gold_Sapphire_Ring "Skyrim:Gold Sapphire Ring") that is easily missed. To the west, past another pillar, are wooden steps leading up to the walkways above. Under the steps are two unusable barrels, a crate, two sacks, a pair of iron boots, and a practice dummy.

Rune totems

The steps lead to a balcony with a riekling hut to the right. Beside the hut are two barrels and two crates, among which are a [chaurus egg](/wiki/Skyrim:Chaurus_Eggs "Skyrim:Chaurus Eggs"), an imp stool sample in a bucket, an apothecary's satchel, and two [charred skeever hides](/wiki/Skyrim:Charred_Skeever_Hide "Skyrim:Charred Skeever Hide"). Opposite is an urn, and farther along is a stone walkway over to the first of the pillars and onward to the second pillar. On your left is a platform built on the side of the pillar, with a piece of [honeycomb](/wiki/Skyrim:Honeycomb "Skyrim:Honeycomb") on a [plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Plate "Skyrim:Plate") on the ground. Another walkway continues to another balcony on the other side of the room. There is another hut on this side, next to which is an open box containing two iron ingots and a flute, with a crate and two barrels beside it. On one barrel is an expert-locked [East Empire Company strongbox](/wiki/Skyrim:East_Empire_Company_Strongbox "Skyrim:East Empire Company Strongbox"), and on the other, which is a fish barrel, is a potato on a plate. Also on this balcony is a sack next to a crate, as well as three garlic bulbs in a bucket, a [leek](/wiki/Skyrim:Leek "Skyrim:Leek"), and a [silver ingot](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Ingot "Skyrim:Silver Ingot"), all by two barrels and a crate. There is also a large piece of stone carved with the symbol of a whale, as generally used for [rune totem](/wiki/Skyrim:Rune_Totems "Skyrim:Rune Totems") puzzles.

On the southern side of the room on ground level, among some rune totems, are some crates with two goblets, a [cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage"), and a bowl with [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender") inside. There is also a gate blocking a doorway in the middle of the southern wall. The symbols needed are above the rune totems, except for the second, which is on the eastern balcony. The handle to operate the gate is on a raised section between two pillars, with lit braziers lighting the area. Once you've lined up the correct symbols (from left to right: **Eagle—Whale—Whale—Snake**), pull the handle to open the gate. Incorrect guesses seem to have no negative repercussions. You can see the word wall through the gate. The wall teaches a word for the Cyclone shout. In front of the wall is an unlocked boss chest.

On the east side of the room with the wall is a cave-in, leaving a ramp up to an opening in the east wall. This leads to a tunnel that twists and turns and eventually opens into a circular room with the *[Black Book: Untold Legends](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Book:_Untold_Legends_(book) "Skyrim:Black Book: Untold Legends (book)")*. There is an iron door to the south leading back to the first zone. Through this door is a small room with two large urns on your left, and a short tunnel ahead leading to a hidden door. The chain to open the door is to the right of the door, and the passage beyond leads you back to the first chest with two burial urns near the exit.

## Notes

- The name *Benkongerike* is a Norwegian compound word, comprising *ben* meaning *bone/leg* and *kongerike* meaning *kingdom*. It can thus be translated as *Bone Kingdom* or *Kingdom of Bones*.
- In [Survival Mode](/wiki/Skyrim:Survival_Mode "Skyrim:Survival Mode"), this dungeon will not warm you up, unlike most interior locations.
- Benkongerike also [appears](/wiki/Bloodmoon:Benkongerike "Bloodmoon:Benkongerike") in *[Bloodmoon](/wiki/Bloodmoon:Bloodmoon "Bloodmoon:Bloodmoon")*.

## Bugs

- There are some items you can't interact with.
  -  The [Unofficial Dragonborn Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dragonborn_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dragonborn Patch"), version 2.0.2, fixes this bug.
- The rune totems may not rotate.
- When Lost Knowledge is the active quest, Clairvoyance and the map marker can direct you to the escape passage even when it hasn't been opened.
- If you reenter *Benkongerike Great Hall* after everything has respawned, the sarcophagus with the stalhrim deposit will appear to have more stalhrim in it. However, when you approach it, you don't get the option to "mine deposit"; you only get the "search draugr" option, as if the deposit was not there. **?**

Benkum

**Benkum** is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") found at the [Water Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Water_Stone "Skyrim:Water Stone") in Solstheim.

Initially from [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm"), Benkum, along with fellow sailors [Liesl](/wiki/Skyrim:Liesl "Skyrim:Liesl"), [Hjalfar](/wiki/Skyrim:Hjalfar "Skyrim:Hjalfar"), and [Palevius Lex](/wiki/Skyrim:Palevius_Lex "Skyrim:Palevius Lex"), decided to cast anchor along the western coast of Solstheim and immediately fell prey to [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak_(person) "Skyrim:Miraak (person)")'s spell. He works around the clock at the stone, oblivious to the world around him. Once the stone has been [cleansed](/wiki/Skyrim:Cleansing_the_Stones "Skyrim:Cleansing the Stones"), the entire crew will return to their boat on the coast. When you leave the area, they will all disappear from the game.

He wears [miner's clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Miner%27s_Clothes#00080697 "Skyrim:Miner's Clothes"), [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Boots#00080699 "Skyrim:Boots"), and [gloves](/wiki/Skyrim:Gloves#000261c1 "Skyrim:Gloves"), and he carries a [steel sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Sword "Skyrim:Steel Sword").

## Dialogue

He shares his dialogue lines with his fellow sailors:

:   *"Think we've got to get back to our ship now."*
:   *"We're already late. Not sure why we decided to take such an extended shore time."*
:   *"When the tide goes, we'll go with it."*
:   *"It's a long way back to Windhelm from here."*
:   *"Hope our shipments are still good. How long has it been?"*
:   *"Best be shoving off now."*

## Notes

- There's an unused NPC in the base game named [Benkum](/wiki/Skyrim:Unused_NPCs#Benkum "Skyrim:Unused NPCs") who was intended to manage the wagers for the removed arena in [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm").

## Bugs

- Benkum and the other sailors are sometimes not removed along with their ship, and are left stranded by the beach down west from the Water Stone.
  -  The [Unofficial Dragonborn Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dragonborn_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dragonborn Patch"), version 1.0.2, fixes this bug.

Benor

The mob outside [Movarth's Lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Movarth%27s_Lair "Skyrim:Movarth's Lair")

**Benor** is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") [warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:CombatWarrior2H "Skyrim:CombatWarrior2H") living in [Morthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Morthal "Skyrim:Morthal"). He claims to be an amazing fighter and is ready to [prove it](/wiki/Skyrim:Fight!_Fight! "Skyrim:Fight! Fight!") for a bet of 100 gold. If you defeat him, he can be recruited as a [follower](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers") and will also be a potential candidate for [marriage](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Bonds_of_Matrimony "Skyrim:The Bonds of Matrimony").

Benor has decided to help out the city watch, so he is allowed to sleep in the [Guardhouse](/wiki/Skyrim:Guardhouse "Skyrim:Guardhouse") every night between 2am and 9am. He then spends nearly all of his time patrolling the town. After waking up, he spends two hours guarding the Guardhouse by standing on the porch outside then heads down to the bridge that leads to the sawmill. When the clock strikes noon, he spends two hours investigating the mysterious [burned-down house](/wiki/Skyrim:Laid_to_Rest "Skyrim:Laid to Rest") in the western part of town. At 2pm he returns to the bridge and at 5pm he heads back to the porch. At 7pm he finally relaxes and heads to the [Moorside Inn](/wiki/Skyrim:Moorside_Inn "Skyrim:Moorside Inn") where he stays until midnight when he heads back to the Guardhouse and paces around until his bedtime.

He wears [iron armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Armor "Skyrim:Iron Armor") with matching [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Boots "Skyrim:Iron Boots") and [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Gauntlets "Skyrim:Iron Gauntlets"). He wields an [iron battleaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Battleaxe "Skyrim:Iron Battleaxe") and carries a selection of [middle-class items and gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Common "Skyrim:Leveled Lists").

## Related Quests

- **[Fight! Fight!](/wiki/Skyrim:Fight!_Fight! "Skyrim:Fight! Fight!")**: Prove your strength by wagering on a fist fight with another. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Laid to Rest](/wiki/Skyrim:Laid_to_Rest "Skyrim:Laid to Rest")**: Investigate a tragic house fire, and discover an insidious plot against the town.

### Fight! Fight!

If you dare question him if he really is the best warrior in town:

:   **Best warrior in Morthal, huh?**
:   *"Want me to prove it? I bet a hundred gold I can take you, bare-handed."*

:   **I've got better things to do.**

    :   *"Milk drinker."*

:   **You're on. (Brawl - 100 gold)**
:   *"Just your own two hands. Weapons and magic are out. Now let's see what you got!"*

Should you accept his bet without 100 gold in your possession:

:   *"Come back when you have the coin."*

When you have defeated him in hand-to-hand, he will get up and say:

:   *"Now that was a punch."*

When he hands you the prize, he will admit:

:   *"You're a real fighter. I like that. You ever need my steel by your side, you just ask."*

## Dialogue

When approached he can say:

:   *"Morthal used to be a quiet place. But then, the world used to make sense."*
:   *"I figure the guards could always use some help, so I keep my eyes open."*
:   *"Been hoping they'd make me a guard, but not yet. Still, I'll help them out if I can."*
:   *"The Jarl does little to protect us these days."*
:   *"You ask me, we'd be better off without that [wizard](/wiki/Skyrim:Falion "Skyrim:Falion") in town."*
:   *"This isn't the time or place for magic, or whatever it is Falion does."*

If you talk to him directly, he will claim:

:   *"I'm the best warrior in Morthal, and that's no boast."*
:   **What is it you do here in town?**
:   *"Oh, well. You know. A bit of this, a bit of that. They haven't made me a guard, even though I've been asking. So I'll take odd jobs, anything that comes along for now."*

## Conversations

When Benor visits the Moorside Inn, he will often hook up with his good friend [Gorm](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm "Skyrim:Gorm") and speak secretly about their dissatisfaction with the Jarl:

:   **Benor**: *"Ho, Gorm."*
:   **Gorm**: *"Buy you a drink?"*
:   **Benor**: *"Not right now. Anything new?"*
:   **Gorm**: *"Still the same. I tell you, something's got to be done."*
:   **Benor**: *"When the time is right, friend. When we're sure."*
:   **Gorm**: *"The longer we wait, the worse it gets."*
:   **Benor**: *"Let's talk about it some other time."*

Like most other men in Morthal, Benor will also occasionally be hit on by the sultry [Alva](/wiki/Skyrim:Alva "Skyrim:Alva"):

:   **Alva**: *"I'm bored, Benor. Nobody wants to have any fun with me."*
:   **Benor**: *"If you leave that kinslayer [Hroggar](/wiki/Skyrim:Hroggar "Skyrim:Hroggar"), I would be happy to keep your company."*
:   **Alva**: *"Hroggar doesn't have to know if we sit together. Or drink together. I doubt he would even care."*
:   **Benor**: *"You tempt me mightily, Alva. But I won't cuckhold*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *another man, even on*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *murderer like Hroggar."*

## Notes

- If Benor is an active follower at the time of Laid to Rest when you have to enter [Movarth's Lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Movarth%27s_Lair "Skyrim:Movarth's Lair"), he will still join the mob. He will rejoin you after the scene outside Movarth's Lair. If you enter Movarth's Lair before talking to the mob outside, he won't follow you in unless you exit and talk to them. If Benor hasn't been recruited by then, you can still do so once the mob retreats.

## Bugs

- If killed, Benor's corpse could persist indefinitely, due to lacking a cleanup script.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
- Benor *should* sleep inside of the guardhouse, but he can't enter it due to not having a key. And even if he had a key, he couldn't sleep inside due to there not being a bed available for him.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.3.3, addresses this issue. ([details](https://afktrack.afkmods.com/index.php?a=issues&i=13063)) A bed has been given to him in the jailhouse level as there was no more room upstairs. His sleep package was adjusted to point to the new bed.

| Voice Type | [FemaleOldGrumpy](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Voice-FemaleOldGrumpy "Category:Skyrim-Voice-FemaleOldGrumpy") | | |
| [Faction(s)](/wiki/Skyrim:Factions "Skyrim:Factions") | [CrimeFactionWhiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:CrimeFactionWhiterun "Skyrim:CrimeFactionWhiterun"); [TownWhiterunFaction](/wiki/Skyrim:TownWhiterunFaction "Skyrim:TownWhiterunFaction"); [Whiterun House Battle-Born Faction](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_House_Battle-Born_Faction "Skyrim:Whiterun House Battle-Born Faction"); [WhiterunMarketShoppers](/wiki/Skyrim:WhiterunMarketShoppers "Skyrim:WhiterunMarketShoppers") | | |

Bergritte Battle-Born

**Bergritte Battle-Born** is an [elderly](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder "Skyrim:Elder") [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") living in the [House of Clan Battle-Born](/wiki/Skyrim:House_of_Clan_Battle-Born "Skyrim:House of Clan Battle-Born") in [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun"). She is the wife of [Olfrid Battle-Born](/wiki/Skyrim:Olfrid_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Olfrid Battle-Born") and has two children, [Jon](/wiki/Skyrim:Jon_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Jon Battle-Born") and [Alfhild](/wiki/Skyrim:Alfhild_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Alfhild Battle-Born"). Alfhild is married to [Idolaf](/wiki/Skyrim:Idolaf_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Idolaf Battle-Born") and they have given Bergritte her first grandchild, [Lars](/wiki/Skyrim:Lars_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Lars Battle-Born").

As family elder, she lives a relatively anonymous existence in Whiterun. She wakes up early at 6am and spends her morning in her favorite chair, eating and relaxing. At noon she heads over to the Gildergreen and listens to [Heimskr](/wiki/Skyrim:Heimskr "Skyrim:Heimskr")'s ramblings until she goes down to the market at 3pm. At 6pm she returns to the house for some dinner before her bedtime at 8pm.

She wears a set of farmer [clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000209a6 "Skyrim:Clothing") with a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000209a5 "Skyrim:Clothing") and a [hat](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000209aa "Skyrim:Clothing"). She carries the [house key](/wiki/Skyrim:Key_to_House_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Key to House Battle-Born"), an [iron dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Dagger "Skyrim:Iron Dagger"), and a selection of [common items and gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Common "Skyrim:Leveled Lists").

## Dialogue

When approached, she will provide some random information, saying:

:   *"There's a rift here in Skyrim, and can't neither magic nor the passin' of time make it right."*
:   *"Evgir Unslaad has come at last. The 'Season Unending.' War... without end."*
:   *"Can you believe those pathetic Gray-Manes still show their face in public?"*
:   *"There was love between our families. For generations. Now, there is only enmity."*
:   *"Do be careful, child. Skyrim is not as safe as it used to be."*
:   *"By the way, you might want to stop in at Warmaiden's. These days, folk need all the protection they can get."*

If Whiterun was conquered by the [Stormcloaks](/wiki/Skyrim:Stormcloaks "Skyrim:Stormcloaks") during [Battle for Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_for_Whiterun_(Stormcloaks) "Skyrim:Battle for Whiterun (Stormcloaks)"), she will hatefully add:

:   *"It's a miracle these Stormcloaks haven't robbed us blind yet. I'm sure it's only a matter of time."*

## Conversations

Bergritte suggests [Lars](/wiki/Skyrim:Lars_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Lars Battle-Born") go play outside:

**Bergritte:** *Lars, dear, why don't you go outside and play? It's a beautiful day.*
**Lars:** *That's all right, grandmother. I like staying home with you.*
**Bergritte:** *It's that Braith girl again, isn't it? Has she been bothering you again? I've a mind to speak with her mother.*
**Lars:** *No! Please, grandmother, don't do that. I'm fine. Really. Can we just... not talk about this anymore?*
**Bergritte:** *All right, dear.*

Bergritte and her daughter, [Alfhild](/wiki/Skyrim:Alfhild_Battle-Born "Skyrim:Alfhild Battle-Born"), discussing reading material:

**Alfhild:** *So, what book should I read to you tonight?*
**Bergritte:** *How about ["The Lusty Argonian Maid"](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Lusty_Argonian_Maid "Skyrim:The Lusty Argonian Maid")?*
**Alfhild:** *Mother!*
**Bergritte:** *You've got no sense of humor, you know that? Why don't you pick up where you left off with ["The Real Barenziah"](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Real_Barenziah "Skyrim:The Real Barenziah").*

Bersi Honey-Hand

**Bersi Honey-Hand** is the [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") owner and vendor of the general goods store [Pawned Prawn](/wiki/Skyrim:Pawned_Prawn "Skyrim:Pawned Prawn") in [Riften](/wiki/Skyrim:Riften "Skyrim:Riften"). His wife [Drifa](/wiki/Skyrim:Drifa "Skyrim:Drifa") lives in the store with him. A former sailor, Bersi used to own a fishing boat, which he named the *Brawny Prawn*. After selling his boat, he named his shop to commemorate his former life.

Like many other citizens of Riften, Bersi is concerned about the rampant corruption within the city. Unlike most, he believes in improving the morality of the citizens through worship at the [Temple of Mara](/wiki/Skyrim:Temple_of_Mara "Skyrim:Temple of Mara"). This has earned him the ridicule of many other citizens, who are convinced that the corruption runs too deep to be removed with prayers.

During the Thieves Guild quest [Taking Care of Business](/wiki/Skyrim:Taking_Care_of_Business "Skyrim:Taking Care of Business"), you are sent to retrieve protection money that Bersi owes the guild. He will agree to pay after being beaten in a brawl or after you destroy one of his prized possessions, a [Dwemer](/wiki/Lore:Dwemer "Lore:Dwemer") urn.

Bersi will begin his day at 6am, having breakfast for two hours. From 8am until 1pm he will man the store, until sitting down with his wife to have lunch at 1pm for an hour. He will then man the store until 6pm, then have dinner for an hour. After this, he will roam around the Riften market until 11pm, browsing the stalls, sitting on the benches, and occasionally using the armor workbench next to [The Scorched Hammer](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Scorched_Hammer "Skyrim:The Scorched Hammer"). From 11pm to midnight, he will stand at the counter in The Pawned Prawn, and at midnight he will go to sleep.

Bersi wears a set of merchant [clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothes#0004223c "Skyrim:Clothes") along with a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Boots#0004223d "Skyrim:Boots"). He carries his [key](/wiki/Skyrim:Pawned_Prawn_Key "Skyrim:Pawned Prawn Key") to the store, a [belted tunic](/wiki/Skyrim:Belted_Tunic "Skyrim:Belted Tunic"), and a selection of [common loot and gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Common "Skyrim:Leveled Lists"). In combat, he relies on a leveled [dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Dagger "Skyrim:Dagger") which can be up to [elven](/wiki/Skyrim:Elven "Skyrim:Elven") in quality.

## Related Quests

- **[Taking Care of Business](/wiki/Skyrim:Taking_Care_of_Business "Skyrim:Taking Care of Business")**: Collect some debts for the [Thieves Guild](/wiki/Skyrim:Thieves_Guild_(faction) "Skyrim:Thieves Guild (faction)").

### Taking Care of Business

When first spoken to:

:   **I have a message from Brynjolf.**
:   *"Wha... what? Oh, it's one of you people. So, Brynjolf doesn't even bother to show up himself anymore, eh? What's this message?"*

:   :   **Simple. You don't pay, bad things happen.**
    :   *"Petty threats and fist waving are not going to sway me. You people are all talk, and everyone knows it! Pay to protect me? You can't even protect yourselves!"*

:   :   **I think you know what it is.**
    :   *"You're gouging me for what little coin I make and you can't even protect yourselves? Ridiculous!"*

Both will lead to:

:   **We can protect ourselves. Trust me.**
:   *"Don't fool yourself. It's only a matter of time before you people are run out of Riften."*

:   :   **I've had enough of this.**
    :   *"Likewise. Now, I have a lot to do, so I'm afraid you'll just have to leave!"*

:   :   **I think you need to shut your mouth. (Brawl)**
    :   *"I'm going to make you sorry for this!"*

If spoken to again before destroying the urn:

:   *"Please, reconsider what you're doing. Maybe I can pay later..."*
:   *"I'm sorry, you're going to have to leave. Tell Brynjolf he'll just have to make due without my coin."*

If you destroy the urn he has:

:   *"No! That urn was priceless!"*
:   **You want me to break anything else?**
:   *"All right! I get it. I'll pay on time from now on. Just don't smash anything else. Here, take your gold and leave me in peace."*

If you decide to brawl and win:

:   *"Please, no more. I'll pay, I'll pay. Here!"*

If you choose to destroy the urn before even speaking to him:

:   **That was from Brynjolf. Get the message?**
:   *"I can't believe you did that. You people are monsters! You demand payment for protection and you can't even protect yourselves. Here, take your coin and tell Brynjolf to leave us alone."*

If you have already collected debts from the other debtors he will instead give you the money:

:   **I have a message from Brynjolf.**
:   *"Oh! There's no need for that. I know why you're here. Tell Brynjolf not to worry about it anymore. Oh! And look, I even have the payment I owed. Here, take it."*

## Dialogue

In his shop, he will greet you with:

:   *"Welcome to the Pawned Prawn. Come on in, take a look around."*
:   *"Welcome to the Pawned Prawn. What can I do for you?"*
:   *"I have all sorts of interesting items for sale. Have you looked around?"*
:   *"Pickings may be a bit slim today, but if you see anything you like I'll make you a good deal."*
:   *"I hope you're here for friendlier reasons now... after all, I'm all paid up."*

Should you meet him outside his shop, he will invite you to the Prawn:

:   *"If you're looking for anything to sell for a fair price, I run the Pawned Prawn over by the market."*

When spoken to directly he can be asked questions about himself and his business:

:   **Your shop has a most unusual name.**
:   *"Catchy, isn't it? In my youth I was a fisherman... I had a beautiful ship named "The Brawny Prawn." But the years have a way of creeping up on you. I ended up selling that ship to open this place. Seemed only fitting to name it after her. Well, changed it a bit I suppose. If I had been smarter, I would have kept my boat. Coming to this city was a big mistake."*

:   **What's wrong with Riften?**
:   *"The question is, what isn't wrong with Riften. This city is corrupt. Rotten to the core. No one cares about anything except themselves and how much coin they can make off the misery of others."*

    :   **Maybe you should speak to the authorities.**
    :   *"Authorities? Have you been listening to what I said? They're all dirty. Every one of them. The only way to get things done in this city is to keep your head down and pay off the right people."*

:   **Tell me about the Thieves Guild.**
:   *"They used to be pretty feared around here. I mean, you'd whisper the name and it'd send chills down your spine. Now, they're nothing more than ruffians and thugs trying to pry a few extra coin from honest people. All it would take is a small force of guard to go into [the Ratway](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Ratway "Skyrim:The Ratway") and flush them out."*

    :   **What's the Ratway?**
    :   *"It's our name for the old sewers that run under the city. It used to be a huge system hundreds of years ago but it fell into decay just like the rest of Riften. The Guild stocks the place full of thugs that aren't good enough to join, so watch yourself if you venture down there."*

## Conversations

Bersi may be seen having random conversations with his wife Drifa:

:   **Bersi**: *"Drifa? I was looking through our books and there's an entry for "spices." Says we spent 300 septims. What is that?"*
:   **Drifa**: *"Spices? I'm certain I have no idea what you're talking about."*
:   **Bersi**: *"You sure? It was in your handwriting. If you can't keep the books straight then let me do them."*
:   **Drifa**: *"Oh, yes... spices. That was a special order for someone in Whiterun. Should be along any day now. Don't let it worry you, my dear."*

:   **Drifa**: *"You keep giving and giving Bersi, and they'll keep taking and taking. When is it going to end?"*
:   **Bersi**: *"What would you have me do, woman? Cross the Guild? Take them all on one by one?"*
:   **Drifa**: *"You know I don't mean that. We need to find a way out of this. Perhaps talk to Laila..."*
:   **Bersi**: *"Laila is as clueless as she is stupid. No. If anything's to be done about this, we have to deal with it ourselves."*

## Notes

- In [Patch 1.5](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch#version_1.5 "Skyrim:Patch") Bersi was added to a new `CR08ExclusionFaction`, preventing him from being a radiantly-selected victim for the [Rescue Mission](/wiki/Skyrim:Rescue_Mission "Skyrim:Rescue Mission") quest.
- If [Drifa](/wiki/Skyrim:Drifa "Skyrim:Drifa") is killed, Bersi can sometimes be seen wearing an [Amulet of Mara](/wiki/Skyrim:Amulet_of_Mara "Skyrim:Amulet of Mara").
- He is marked as a confidant to [Lynly Star-Sung](/wiki/Skyrim:Lynly_Star-Sung "Skyrim:Lynly Star-Sung") despite no apparent connection between the two.
  - He is at least acquainted with [Wilhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Wilhelm "Skyrim:Wilhelm"). The letter *[An Apology](/wiki/Skyrim:An_Apology "Skyrim:An Apology")* implies Bersi had previously asked him to loot [Shroud Hearth Barrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Shroud_Hearth_Barrow "Skyrim:Shroud Hearth Barrow") for any ancient Nord artifacts to sell.
- His efforts to spread the teachings of Mara often bother his wife, who often laments, *"My husband Bersi will be the death of me. He spends too much time worrying about the city, and not enough about himself."*

Betrid Silver-Blood reading

**Betrid Silver-Blood** is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") [citizen](/wiki/Skyrim:Citizen_(class) "Skyrim:Citizen (class)") who lives at [the Treasury House](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Treasury_House "Skyrim:The Treasury House") in [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth"). Her husband is the influential head of the Silver-Blood family, [Thonar](/wiki/Skyrim:Thonar_Silver-Blood "Skyrim:Thonar Silver-Blood"), whom she only married for the money.

Before the [related quest](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Forsworn_Conspiracy "Skyrim:The Forsworn Conspiracy"), all her time is spent reading in a chair at the Treasury House. If you choose to question Thonar as part of your investigation, she is killed by [Nana Ildene](/wiki/Skyrim:Nana_Ildene "Skyrim:Nana Ildene") in a scripted death. If you choose not to question Thonar (see [notes](#Notes)) she will survive the quest and, once you have [escaped](/wiki/Skyrim:No_One_Escapes_Cidhna_Mine "Skyrim:No One Escapes Cidhna Mine") from [Cidhna Mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Cidhna_Mine "Skyrim:Cidhna Mine"), she will have picked up her daily routine.

She sleeps in the northwestern bedroom every night between 10pm and 6am. After waking up she spends the entire day strolling around, either eating, cooking, relaxing, or reading her book. At 9am and 8pm she pauses for a one-hour meal.

She wears a set of [fine clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#00086991 "Skyrim:Clothing") and a pair of [fine boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#00086993 "Skyrim:Clothing"), and is equipped with an [iron dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Dagger "Skyrim:Iron Dagger"). She carries a [key](/wiki/Skyrim:Key_to_Markarth_Treasury_House "Skyrim:Key to Markarth Treasury House") to the Treasury House and a selection of [higher-class loot and gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Rich "Skyrim:Leveled Lists").

## Related Quests

- **[The Forsworn Conspiracy](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Forsworn_Conspiracy "Skyrim:The Forsworn Conspiracy")**: Investigate a murder in [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth") to discover a sinister plot surrounding the [Forsworn](/wiki/Skyrim:Forsworn "Skyrim:Forsworn").

## Dialogue

She is overly snobbish and will readily tell you about her status when approached. You can ask her questions about her family.

:   *"I'm married to Thonar Silver-Blood. Keep that in mind while you're speaking to me."*

:   *"My husband Thonar handles all our family's business. He's an important man."*

:   *"I married Thonar for the money, and I'm not the least bit ashamed to admit it."*
:   **You're an important family, I take it?**

    :   *"My dear vagrant, we're the only family worth knowing in Markarth. We own everything in this city, even the jail. And guess who owns the [Silver-Blood Inn](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver-Blood_Inn "Skyrim:Silver-Blood Inn")? Not that we named it that, the people just insisted."*
:   **You're married to Thonar? What's he like?**

    :   *"He's the real head of this family. He may not be the eldest, but all the work that keeps us respected is handled by my Thonar."*

When exiting conversation she can say:

:   *"Yes, I was bored talking to you anyway."*

:   *"Take care."*

### Conversations

She will occasionally engage in conversation with her husband:

:   **Betrid**: *"Where were you last night, Thonar? Busy with work or have you found some other woman who's willing to tolerate your lack of ambition?"*
:   **Thonar**: *"I am busy keeping this family in coin and your pretty little head adorned with jewels, so I'll thank you not to question where I go at night, wife."*
:   **Betrid**: *"Well maybe if you would finally convince Thongvor to put you in charge of the family, I wouldn't need to question you anymore."*
:   **Thonar**: *"I'll take control of the family on my own time, Betrid. Until then, my brother remains in charge and you'll keep your mouth shut."*
:   **Betrid**: *"Oh dear, whatever is a girl to do with such fearful brutes about her?"*

:   **Betrid**: *"Did I hear correctly, Thonar? Is your brother really asking you to settle another dispute between [Mulush](/wiki/Skyrim:Mulush_gro-Shugurz "Skyrim:Mulush gro-Shugurz") and [Nepos](/wiki/Skyrim:Nepos_the_Nose "Skyrim:Nepos the Nose")?"*
:   **Thonar**: *"Someone has to keep the silver production running, Betrid, and that means keeping Mulush and Nepos in line once in a while."*
:   **Betrid**: *"Humph. Who's running the Silver-Bloods? You or your brother? You need to tell [Thongvor](/wiki/Skyrim:Thongvor_Silver-Blood "Skyrim:Thongvor Silver-Blood") that he should settle this himself or step down."*
:   **Thonar**: *"The only thing I need to do, dear wife, is make sure profits are up, no matter what. If Thongvor won't do the dirty work, I will."*
:   **Betrid**: *"You'll never be in charge of this family with that attitude, loving husband."*

During a conversation with [Rhiada](/wiki/Skyrim:Rhiada "Skyrim:Rhiada"), Betrid will accidentally reveal a well-kept secret from her past:

:   **Betrid**: *"Rhiada, did you clean the tables today? They're filthy!"*
:   **Rhiada**: *"I'm sorry, Betrid. I'll clean them right away."*
:   **Betrid**: *"No, don't bother. You're useless, as always. I'll get [Ildene](/wiki/Skyrim:Nana_Ildene "Skyrim:Nana Ildene") to do it."*
:   **Rhiada**: *"I'm sorry, Betrid. I thought I had cleaned the tables properly."*
:   **Betrid**: *"Oh, stop apologizing. It makes you look like an idiot. Learn to talk back a bit, girl! Why, when I was in the temple...."*
:   **Rhiada**: *"The temple, Betrid? You were one of Dibella's faithful?"*
:   **Betrid**: *"I misspoke. Never mind what I said. Now get back to work."*

## Unused Dialogue

Betrid has unused dialogue tied to multiple [quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Unfinished_Quests "Skyrim:Unfinished Quests") she was once meant to give you or play a role in. This dialogue can only be found in the game's DialogueViews files, and not the Creation Kit.

### FreeformMarkarthF

This quest would be started by talking to [Lisbet](/wiki/Skyrim:Lisbet "Skyrim:Lisbet"). She would ask you to deliver a letter to Betrid, and warns you that she will not be happy with its contents.

:   **I have a letter from Lisbet.**
:   *"What's this? Some plea for alms for that beggar of a store she runs? Why that... daedra-cavorting harlot. You haven't read this letter, have you?"*

You would then get multiple options, with all of them apparently leading to the same result:

| Topic | Dialogue |
| --- | --- |
| **Yes, I did.**   **Yes, I did. (Lie)**   **No, I haven't.**   **No, I haven't. (Lie)** | *"Well keep quiet and tell Lisbet I'll take care of things. Now get out of my sight."* |

### FreeformMarkarthK

In this quest, Betrid would ask you to deliver a note to [Kleppr](/wiki/Skyrim:Kleppr "Skyrim:Kleppr") at the [Silver-Blood Inn](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver-Blood_Inn "Skyrim:Silver-Blood Inn"). However, her initial dialogue for this isn't present. Her lines upon returning are, however.

:   **I delivered your note.**
:   *"Always good to make sure people know their place, don't you think? Now why don't you take a few coins and run along. Oh, wait, I was going to introduce you to my husband. Just tell him I sent you, and he'll find some way to put you to work."*

## Notes

- Betrid's death can be avoided by pickpocketing and reading [Thonar's journal](/wiki/Skyrim:Thonar%27s_Journal "Skyrim:Thonar's Journal") instead of questioning him.
  - Alternatively, it can be avoided by going directly to [Eltrys](/wiki/Skyrim:Eltrys "Skyrim:Eltrys") after questioning [Nepos the Nose](/wiki/Skyrim:Nepos_the_Nose "Skyrim:Nepos the Nose").
- If you kill Donnel, Rhiada and Nana Ildene before talking to Thonar, she will spontaneously die with no direct cause anyway, prompting Thonar to comment that the Forsworn killed her, even though her intended murderers are already dead.
- The scenes [Hroki](/wiki/Skyrim:Hroki "Skyrim:Hroki") has with [Hogni Red-Arm](/wiki/Skyrim:Hogni_Red-Arm "Skyrim:Hogni Red-Arm") and [Kerah](/wiki/Skyrim:Kerah "Skyrim:Kerah") in the marketplace all internally refer to Betrid instead, suggesting they were originally written for her.
- Internally, Betrid is marked as a rival of [Hamal](/wiki/Skyrim:Hamal "Skyrim:Hamal"). Seeing as Betrid once served at the Temple, it's possible there's bad blood between the two, although neither woman ever mentions the other.

# Skyrim:Beyond Death

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| [SR-qico-Dawnguard Dawnguard.png](/wiki/File:SR-qico-Dawnguard_Dawnguard.png) | **Search for [Valerica](/wiki/Skyrim:Valerica "Skyrim:Valerica") in the [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn").** |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | Automatic upon entering the [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn") during [Chasing Echoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Chasing_Echoes "Skyrim:Chasing Echoes") |
| Location(s): | The [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn") |
| Reward: | [Summon Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Summon_Durnehviir "Skyrim:Summon Durnehviir") shout [Elder Scroll (Blood)](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Scroll_(Blood) "Skyrim:Elder Scroll (Blood)") Camp at [Dayspring Canyon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dayspring_Canyon "Skyrim:Dayspring Canyon") |
| ID: | DLC1VQ05 |
| Suggested Level: | 13 |
| --- | |
| |  |  |  | | --- | --- | --- | | **← Previous** [Chasing Echoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Chasing_Echoes "Skyrim:Chasing Echoes") | **Concurrent** [Seeking Disclosure](/wiki/Skyrim:Seeking_Disclosure "Skyrim:Seeking Disclosure") |  | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | ← Previous | [Chasing Echoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Chasing_Echoes "Skyrim:Chasing Echoes") | | Concurrent | [Seeking Disclosure](/wiki/Skyrim:Seeking_Disclosure "Skyrim:Seeking Disclosure") | | |

[Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)")

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Locate [Valerica](/wiki/Skyrim:Valerica "Skyrim:Valerica").
2. Kill the [Boneyard Keepers](/wiki/Skyrim:Keeper "Skyrim:Keeper").
3. Follow Valerica.
4. Slay [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)").
5. Retrieve the [Elder Scroll](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Scroll_(Blood) "Skyrim:Elder Scroll (Blood)").
6. (If not a vampire) Retrieve the [Soul Essence Gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Essence_Gem "Skyrim:Soul Essence Gem"). (Misc. objective)

### My Mother's Keeper

[Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana") fighting a [Keeper](/wiki/Skyrim:Keeper "Skyrim:Keeper")

Upon your arrival in the [Soul Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn "Skyrim:Soul Cairn"), follow the quest marker to the Boneyard and find [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana")'s mother [Valerica](/wiki/Skyrim:Valerica "Skyrim:Valerica") standing near the entrance. She is initially surprised to find her daughter in the Cairn, before turning her focus on you and your motives for accompanying Serana. Once Serana has interceded for you, Valerica reveals she is still in possession of the [*Blood* Elder Scroll](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Scroll_(Blood) "Skyrim:Elder Scroll (Blood)"). However, she is trapped in the Boneyard by an invisible barrier after fighting with the [Ideal Masters](/wiki/Lore:Ideal_Masters "Lore:Ideal Masters") and their minions when first arriving in the Cairn.

To release her, she directs you to defeat the three [Boneyard Keepers](/wiki/Skyrim:Keeper "Skyrim:Keeper") located across the Cairn. The Keepers each live in separate towers, set apart from the main Boneyard and relatively far apart. The easiest way to navigate to them is by following the three quest markers. Alternatively, if you already killed all 3 Keepers before meeting Valerica, she explains what their purpose was, and will thank you for lifting the barrier.

Each of the Keepers is accompanied by 1-4 minions ([bonemen](/wiki/Skyrim:Boneman "Skyrim:Boneman"), [mistmen](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistman "Skyrim:Mistman") or [wrathmen](/wiki/Skyrim:Wrathman "Skyrim:Wrathman")) that will attack you, usually ahead of your encounter with the Keeper. The Keepers themselves may prove quite a challenge to lower level players, so make full use of Serana's fighting capabilities. One possible strategy for the bow-wielding Keeper is to use [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") to blast it off the edge of the tower.

### Dealing with the Dragon

Once the final Keeper is defeated, return to Valerica. The invisible barrier has now been removed, allowing her to lead you into the Boneyard itself. Once inside, the dragon [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)") will appear and immediately attack you, supported by a host of bonemen. Once he has been defeated, head to the alcove in the southeast corner, where you will find the Elder Scroll surrounded by a number of potions, ingredients and books.

Once you leave the Boneyard from the southwest gate, Durnehviir will rematerialize on top of a nearby stone arch and speak to you, starting [his quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(quest) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (quest)"). If you tell him you have more pressing matters to attend to, his quest will not begin and you will need to return to him at a later time to initiate it. If you are a vampire, simply head southwest back to the portal; if you are not, see the section below.

### Scattered Soul

If you are not a vampire and allowed Serana to partially soul trap you in order to enter the Soul Cairn, you will first need to retrieve your soul from a [Soul Essence Gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Essence_Gem "Skyrim:Soul Essence Gem"). As Valerica explains, this is located at an offering altar not far away. After exiting the Boneyard from the southwest gate, head west-northwest until you reach a fort-like structure with an entrance on the south side. Follow the winding corridor, dispatching the odd [wrathman](/wiki/Skyrim:Wrathman "Skyrim:Wrathman") before emerging into an exterior area. From here head south and east back inside the fort and follow the corridor due north. At the second junction leading east you will find a portal, which takes you outside on the top of the fort. On a raised platform you will find the Soul Essence Gem; once you take it a [Black Soul Gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Soul_Gem "Skyrim:Black Soul Gem") will be added to your inventory and you will start emanating a shaft of bright blue light. Alternatively, you can retrieve the Essence Gem before meeting Valerica, which will immediately result in the negative effect being removed. You can now exit the fort, head south towards the breach in the Cairn walls and then southwest to the portal back to [Castle Volkihar](/wiki/Skyrim:Castle_Volkihar "Skyrim:Castle Volkihar").

### Achievements

One [achievement](/wiki/Skyrim:Achievements "Skyrim:Achievements") is unlocked when you complete this quest:

-  **Beyond Death**[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") (20 points/Bronze)

## Notes

- During this quest, a makeshift camp in [Dayspring Canyon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dayspring_Canyon "Skyrim:Dayspring Canyon") will be set up, with [Alvide](/wiki/Skyrim:Alvide "Skyrim:Alvide"), [Barknar](/wiki/Skyrim:Barknar_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Barknar (Dawnguard)"), [Jayri](/wiki/Skyrim:Jayri "Skyrim:Jayri"), and [Sern](/wiki/Skyrim:Sern "Skyrim:Sern") occupying it.
- While this quest or [Chasing Echoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Chasing_Echoes "Skyrim:Chasing Echoes") are active, you will be unable to dismiss Serana from your party. If you are on the Dawnguard side and a [werewolf](/wiki/Skyrim:Lycanthropy "Skyrim:Lycanthropy"), it can be challenging to use Beast Form and have the Savage Feeding perk as Serana tends to raise corpses in battle. This prevents you from feeding unless you manage to feed on raised corpses after they die again but before they turn into a pile of ash.
- If you defeated [Alduin](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin "Skyrim:Alduin") and finished [Dragonslayer](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonslayer "Skyrim:Dragonslayer") before starting this quest, Durnehviir will be impressed and say *"Even in the Soul Cairn, the defeat of the World Eater has reached my ears, Dovahkiin. You may not be dovah, but the defeat of Alduin earns you the right of title."*
- Given the vastness of the Soul Cairn, [learning](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn_Horse_Quest "Skyrim:Soul Cairn Horse Quest") how to [summon Arvak](/wiki/Skyrim:Summon_Arvak "Skyrim:Summon Arvak") is recommended.
- While Valerica instructs you to retrieve the Soul Gem Essence if you are not a vampire, it is also possible to simply exit the Cairn and complete this quest, which will result in the [Weakened Soul](/wiki/Skyrim:Weakened_Soul "Skyrim:Weakened Soul") effect being removed.
- The soul essence gem can be retrieved before talking to Valerica. If you do so, she won't talk about it.
- It is possible to kill the Keepers before talking to Valerica the first time which unlocks a new line of dialogue from her about it. In order to find the Keepers it is a good idea to look at the top of the buildings until you spot ones with debris swirling around the top of them; the only other building that has this look is Valerica's prison.
- If you sided with the Volkihar, but cured yourself of vampirism before entering the Soul Cairn, Valerica will still refer to you as a vampire.

## Bugs

- After you kill Durnehviir, there will be a prompt to search him but it is impossible to do so.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch") fixes this bug.
- Sometimes after you retrieve your fragmented soul, the stairs leading back to Volkihar Castle on the return trip will be unusable and be part pixelated and you will walk right through them. Re-load a previous save to correct. **?**
- Immediately upon leaving the Boneyard, it is possible to attack Durnehviir before he begins dialogue with you. This may make him hostile or at least prevent dialogue from occurring, making it impossible to obtain the "Summon Durnehviir" shout and by extension the "Soul Tear" shout.
- Valerica will sometimes not move when you return to her after killing the Boneyard Keepers.
  -  Enter the Boneyard and defeat Durnehviir, press the "~" key to open console, and type `tcl` then press enter. You should be able to fly and move through objects; go to the Elder Scroll case and enter the container to pick up the scroll. This will trigger the next stage of the quest, and solve the bug without creating the later bug in the quest [Unseen Visions](/wiki/Skyrim:Unseen_Visions "Skyrim:Unseen Visions").
  -  Another way of solving this is to go into Boneyard and type `prid xx003B8E` first and then `moveto player` . This will teleport Valerica next to you, and she will resume to her correct pathing. As for Serana, just repeat the process but type `prid xx002B74` instead.
- Valerica will not give the dialogue to help you find the soul essence gem if you have already slain one or more of the keepers before talking to her. It is in a building near the westernmost keeper, the one that uses a one-handed weapon and a shield.
  - The chest that contains the soul essence gem can be reached by typing `player.moveto xx00EA8D` . Beware that the chest is directly under one of the health-draining crystals, so this should not be done while low on health.
- The mission can break if you go after the pages of Jiub's Opus and Arvak's Skull causing Serana to disappear and prevent you from furthering and completing the Dawnguard quest line. It is advised to complete the main quests in the Soul Cairn before going after them or walking everywhere in there so as not to lose Serana.
  - To get Serana back, simply go back through the portal to Volkihar. She should appear with you again, and you can then return to the Soul Cairn.
  - If Serana does not reappear in Castle Volkihar Ruins then exit through the door to Castle Volkihar Balcony, open the map and fast travel to Castle Volkihar Blacony again. She should appear next to you.
  -  The console commands `prid xx002B74` and `moveto player` will teleport Serana to you.
- Serana may not give you the Elder Scroll. **?**

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage DLC1VQ05 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest DLC1VQ05`.

# Skyrim:Beyond the Grave

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Visit Edward's Grave.
2. Read the Khajiit's Note.
3. Investigate Knifepoint Ridge.
4. Retrieve the armor.

## Detailed Walkthrough

You can begin this quest by going into the [Dragonsreach Dungeon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonsreach#Dragonsreach_Dungeon "Skyrim:Dragonsreach") in [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun"). On a table just within the jail area find a journal called *[Death of a Crimson Dirk](/wiki/Skyrim:Death_of_a_Crimson_Dirk "Skyrim:Death of a Crimson Dirk")*. Following the directions given in the journal, travel to [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath") in search of the grave of Edward. Your search can be slightly accelerated by looking for the dug up grave with a dead Khajiit nearby. Retrieve the *[Khajiit's Note](/wiki/Skyrim:Khajiit%27s_Note "Skyrim:Khajiit's Note")* from his corpse to determine your next destination, [Knifepoint Ridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Knifepoint_Ridge "Skyrim:Knifepoint Ridge"). The local bandits of the exterior camp will be hostile to you, and will protect your final target for this quest, the "bounty hunter" figure wearing the [Daedric Plate Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedric_Plate_Armor "Skyrim:Daedric Plate Armor") mentioned in the note. Defeat him and any bandits that get in your way to retrieve the set. Read the *[Bounty Hunter's Note](/wiki/Skyrim:Bounty_Hunter%27s_Note "Skyrim:Bounty Hunter's Note")* you can find on the body for confirmation of Edward's scheme.

## Quest Stages

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage ccBGSSSE050_Quest stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest ccBGSSSE050_Quest`.

Big Laborer

The **Big Laborer** is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") [warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:Warrior_(class) "Skyrim:Warrior (class)") that may appear as a target during the quest [The Dark Brotherhood Forever](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Dark_Brotherhood_Forever "Skyrim:The Dark Brotherhood Forever") at [Katla's Farm](/wiki/Skyrim:Katla%27s_Farm "Skyrim:Katla's Farm").

The Big Laborer wears farm [clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000261C0 "Skyrim:Clothing") along with a pair of [boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000261BD "Skyrim:Clothing") and a pair of [gloves](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000261c1 "Skyrim:Clothing").

## Related Quests

- **[The Dark Brotherhood Forever](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Dark_Brotherhood_Forever "Skyrim:The Dark Brotherhood Forever")**: Yet another child has prayed to their [mother](/wiki/Skyrim:Night_Mother "Skyrim:Night Mother").

### The Dark Brotherhood Forever

If spoken to he will say:

:   *"Would it kill you to let a man go about his business in peace? Really, the nerve..."*

Bilegulch Mine

**Bilegulch Mine** is a small [orichalcum](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum "Skyrim:Orichalcum") [mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Mines "Skyrim:Mines") northwest of [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath") containing [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") [bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit"). It contains only one zone, *[Bilegulch Mine](#Bilegulch_Mine)*.

## Related Quests

- **[Amulet of the Moon](/wiki/Skyrim:Amulet_of_the_Moon "Skyrim:Amulet of the Moon")**: Find the [Moon Amulet](/wiki/Skyrim:Moon_Amulet "Skyrim:Moon Amulet") for [Kharjo](/wiki/Skyrim:Kharjo "Skyrim:Kharjo"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Bandit Attack](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit_Attack "Skyrim:Bandit Attack")**[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire"): Rescue your beloved from kidnappers. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Kill the Bandit Leader](/wiki/Skyrim:Kill_the_Bandit_Leader_(Jarl) "Skyrim:Kill the Bandit Leader (Jarl)")**: Slay a [bandit](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit") leader for [Siddgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Siddgeir "Skyrim:Siddgeir"), the [Jarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Jarl "Skyrim:Jarl") of [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

- This location is one of many potential targets for [one or more of the Radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant#Quest_Locations "Skyrim:Radiant").

### Exterior

Mining camp

The mining camp is barricaded and guarded by only a few Orc bandits. A lookout platform, with an Orc bandit on watch, is inside and to the right of the camp entrance. The camp is dotted with a few Orc-styled outbuildings. Immediately to the left of the entrance is one such structure holding a random leveled potion of [attribute](/wiki/Skyrim:Attributes "Skyrim:Attributes") healing, a [potion of true shot](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_True_Shot "Skyrim:Potion of True Shot"), and two leather strips. On the other side of the structure is a basket with six iron arrows, and a low table with three [long bows](/wiki/Skyrim:Long_Bow "Skyrim:Long Bow"), two sheaves of iron arrows, and a sheaf of [Orcish arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish_Arrow "Skyrim:Orcish Arrow"). To the east is another basic structure covering a bedroll, with a level-locked chest and a pair of hide boots next to the structure.

Several sets of stairs supported by scaffolding opposite the camp gate lead up to an area with another bandit and three barrels, one of which can be looted. The entrance to the mine is to the north; with *[Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire")* installed, a [stone quarry](/wiki/Skyrim:Stone_Quarry "Skyrim:Stone Quarry") is just south of the entrance. Two more structures and a final bandit are past the entrance to the east. The structure against the rock face holds a [forge](/wiki/Skyrim:Forge "Skyrim:Forge"), with a [smelter](/wiki/Skyrim:Smelter "Skyrim:Smelter") just to the west; the final bandit is usually working the forge if they haven't detected you. A cart west of the smelter holds six pieces of [orichalcum ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore"). To the east of the forge is a wood-floored area with a [workbench](/wiki/Skyrim:Workbench "Skyrim:Workbench") and a table. On the table is an Orcish greatsword, three pairs of iron gauntlets, two steel swords, and the level-dependent appearance of an Orcish helmet. A steel warhammer leans against the far end of the table. The structure south of the blacksmithing area holds a bedroll and a novice-locked chest that may contain some interesting items. To the west is a table and chair on a small wooden overhang. On the table is a leg of goat roast, a wooden bowl with two green apples, and a bottle of nord mead.

### Bilegulch Mine

[Bone chimes](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Chimes "Skyrim:Bone Chimes") hang just inside the entrance, so move carefully to avoid them, and stealthily if you want to surprise the Orc [bandit chief](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit_Chief "Skyrim:Bandit Chief"). Directly ahead, just behind a wooden cart, is the first of the nine [orichalcum ore veins](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore Vein"), as well as a [pickaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickaxe "Skyrim:Pickaxe") on the ground to the left. On a round table close by is an open crate with three bottles of [Nord mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord_Mead "Skyrim:Nord Mead"). The mine turns left before the cart, and you will likely see the bandit chief straight ahead now. Before advancing, look to the crates on the left-hand side for another open crate holding a [leek](/wiki/Skyrim:Leek "Skyrim:Leek"), a [draught of the knight](/wiki/Skyrim:Draught_of_the_Knight "Skyrim:Draught of the Knight"), and a [draught of resist magic](/wiki/Skyrim:Draught_of_Resist_Magic "Skyrim:Draught of Resist Magic"). There is a barrel just after them that can be looted for minor gains, and a second ore vein is on the wall to the right.

Bandit chief's area

The mine now splits into two paths; to the left the mine drops down to another level, while the path straight ahead soon turns left to the chief's camp. The chief's camp contains an expert-locked chest that can be opened with the [Bilegulch Mine key](/wiki/Skyrim:Bilegulch_Mine_Key "Skyrim:Bilegulch Mine Key") (held by the bandit chief), another barrel, a table with some food, and a bedroll. On the table is a leg of goat roast, some [raw beef](/wiki/Skyrim:Raw_Beef "Skyrim:Raw Beef"), a bottle of wine, and a [woodcutter's axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Woodcutter%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Woodcutter's Axe").

The path that drops down to the next level contains some more bone chimes, which you may want to avoid if the chief has wandered down there and you wish to catch them off-guard. At the bottom of the ramp is a broken cart and a table with a copy of the [Smithing](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[The Armorer's Challenge](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Armorer%27s_Challenge "Skyrim:The Armorer's Challenge")*, two shovels, and three pickaxes. The last room contains the seven remaining ore veins (four on the left, three on the right), another lootable barrel, and a cart.

## Notes

- Bilegulch Mine was once meant to be attached to an [Orc stronghold](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds") known as **Makbur**. Three markers still present outside the mine refer to Makbur: `MakburSmelterMarker`, `MakburCenterMarkerREF`, and `MakburBlacksmithMarker`.
  - The game's DialogueViews files also contain a mention of Makbur. The files show that the gate guards for all strongholds were once meant to give you a small bit of info about their respective home. In the final game, however, these lines were replaced by a singular line mentioning all strongholds at once. Makbur's line would've been: *"We call our stronghold Makbur, ruled by chief Shammak, descended of the great founders."*
  - Bilegulch still contains many Orcish themes. It contains the highest overall concentrated quantity of orichalcum (both in the number of available veins, as well as the overall number of ore), the key component in [Orcish](/wiki/Skyrim:Orcish "Skyrim:Orcish") weapons and armor, in the game; all bandits in and around the mine are set to spawn as Orcs; and the surrounding architecture resembles that which you would expect to find in an Orc stronghold, albeit without a longhouse. It's unknown if this layout was repurposed from the original vision of the stronghold, or if the designers added Orcish elements to the mine in reference to its former appearance.

## Maps

- 

  Bilegulch Mine

# Skyrim:Birna's Oddments

## Overview

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
